Thought:
  The median is the middle value of a set of numbers.
  If the median income is $3000, it means that there are people in the family that earn less than $3000 and people who earn more.
  We know that the total income of the family is $9000.
  If the median income is $3000, then there are an equal number of people who earn less than $3000 and an equal number of people who earn more.
  Let's assume that there are "x" number of people who earn less than $3000 and "y" number of people who earn more than $3000.
  The median income is the average of the middle two values when the data is arranged in order.
  Since the median income is $3000, we can say that:
  x * p + y * q = $3000 (where p is the average income of those who earn less than $3000 and q is the average income of those who earn more than $3000)
  Also, we know that the total income of the family is $9000, so:
  x * p + y * q = $9000
  We can solve these two equations simultaneously to get the value of x and y.

Calculation:
  Let's assume that there are "n" number of people in the family.
  If "n" is odd, then the median income will be the income of the middle person.
  If "n" is even, then the median income will be the average of the incomes of the two middle people.
  We are given that the median income is $3000, so we can assume that there are "n" people in the family and the median income is the income of the (n/2)+1 th person.
  Let's assume that there are "x" people in the family who earn less than $3000.
  So, there are (n-x) people who earn more than $3000.
  We can assume that the average income of those who earn less than $3000 is "p" and the average income of those who earn more than $3000 is "q".
  We have two equations:
  x * p + (n-x) * q = $9000  (total income of the family)
  x < (n/2)+1, and (n-x) < (n/2)+1  (since the median income is $3000)

  We can simplify the first equation to get:
  q = (9000 - x*p) / (n-x)

  We can substitute this value of q in the second equation to get:
  x * p + (n-x) * ((9000 - x*p) / (n-x)) = $3000

  Simplifying this equation, we get:
  x * p + 9000 - x * p = $3000
  9000 = $3000
  This is not possible, so we made some mistake in the assumption.

Thought:
  We have made a mistake in the assumption that there are equal number of people who earn less than and more than $3000.
  We can try other assumptions:
  Let's assume that there are "x" number of people who earn less than $3000 and "y" number of people who earn more than $3000, where x is not equal to y.
  We can assume that the incomes of those who earn less than $3000 are arranged in increasing order and the incomes of those who earn more than $3000 are arranged in decreasing order.
  We are given that the median income is $3000, so we can assume that:
  The (x+1)th person earns $3000 and the (y-1)th person also earns $3000.

  We are given that the total income of the family is $9000, so:
  x * p + y * q = $9000  (where p is the average income of those who earn less than $3000 and q is the average income of those who earn more than $3000)
  We can also say that:
  x * a + y * b = $9000
  We have 2 equations and 2 variables, so we can solve for x and y.

Calculation:
  Let's assume that there are "x" people who earn less than $3000 and "y" people who earn more than $3000.
  We can assume that the incomes of those who earn less than $3000 are arranged in increasing order and the incomes of those who earn more than $3000 are arranged in decreasing order.
  We are given that the median income is $3000, so we can assume that:
  The (x+1)th person earns $3000 and the (y-1)th person also earns $3000.
  Let's say that the income of the (x+1)th person is "a" and the income of the (y-1)th person is "b".
  We can assume that:
  a < $3000 < b  (since we arranged the incomes in increasing and decreasing order)

  We know that the total income of the family is $9000, so:
  x * p + y * q = $9000

  We can also say that:
  x * a + y * b = $9000

  We have 2 equations and 2 variables, so we can solve for x and y.
  We can rearrange the first equation to get:
  p = (9000 - y * q) / x

  We can substitute this value of p in the second equation to get:
  x * a + y * b = $9000
  x * a + y * b = $9000 - y * ((9000 - y * q) / x)

  Simplifying this equation, we get:
  x * a * x + y * b * x = 9000 * x - y * (9000 - y * q)
  x * a * x + y * b * x + y * (9000 - y * q) = 9000 * x
  x * (a * x + y * b + 9000 - y * q) = 9000 * x
  a * x + y * b + 9000 - y * q = 9000
  a * x + y * (b - q) = 0
  y = -a * x / (b - q)
  We can substitute this value of y in the first equation to get:
  x * p - x * q * a / (b - q) = $9000

  Simplifying this equation, we get:
  x * (p - q * a / (b - q)) = $9000
  x = $9000 / (p - q * a / (b - q))

  We can substitute the values of p, q, a and b in this equation to get the value of x.
  Let's try different values of a and b to see which values work.
  If a = $1000 and b = $5000:
  q = (9000 - x * p) / y = (9000 - 1000 * (x+1) - 5000 * (y-1)) / (x+y) = (1000 - 4000y) / (x+y)
  x = $9000 / (p - q * a / (b - q)) = $9000 / (a + q) = 9000 / (1000 + (1000 - 4000y) / (x+y))
  This equation gives x = 4, which means that there are 4 people in the family.
  The answer is C: 4.

Question: A starts a business with Rs.40,000. After 2 months, B joined him with Rs.60,000. C joined them after some more time with Rs.120,000. At the end of the year, out of a total profit of Rs.375,000, C gets Rs.150,000 as his share. How many months after B joined the business, did C join?
Choices:
  A: 2 months
  B: 4 months
  C: 23 months
  D: 24 months
  E: 84 months
Response 0:
Thought: 
  Total investment of A and B is Rs.(40000 x 12 + 60000 x 10) = Rs.12,00,000
  C's share of Rs.150,000 is [150000/375000] of the total profit
  So, the total profit is Rs.(150000 x 4) = Rs.600,000
  A and B's share of the profit is Rs.(600000 - 150000) = Rs.450,000
  A's profit share in 12 months = Rs.(40000 x 12 / 1200000 x 450000) = Rs.45,000
  B's profit share in 10 months = Rs.(60000 x 10 / 1200000 x 450000) = Rs.37,500
  C's profit share in 2 months = Rs.(120000 x 2 / 1200000 x 450000) = Rs.4,000
  Let x be the number of months after B joined the business when C joined.
  So, C's profit share is [x + (12-x-10) + 2] / 12 x 450000 = Rs.150,000
  Solving this equation, we get x = 4
  Therefore, C joined the business 4 months after B.
  The answer is B: 4 months.

Question: The monthly salary S of a shop assistant is the sum of a fixed salary of $500 plus 5% of all monthly sales. What should the monthly sales be so that her monthly salary reaches $1500?
Choices:
  A: $50000
  B: $40000
  C: $30000
  D: $20000
  E: None of these

  So, we need to solve for sales in the equation S = 500 + 0.05s = 1500.
  By solving the equation, we get s = (1500 - 500) / 0.05 = 20000.
  Therefore, the monthly sales should be $20000.

Question: The sum of k consecutive integers is 51. If the least integer is -50, then k =
Choices:
  A: 40
  B: 62
  C: 82
  D: 92
  E: 102
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's assume that there are k consecutive integers starting from -50.
  The sum of these integers will be (k/2)(first integer + last integer).
  Since the first integer is -50, the last integer can be found by adding k-1 to -50.
  Therefore, the sum of k consecutive integers starting from -50 is (k/2)(-50+(-50+k-1))= (k/2)(2k-51).
  We know that the sum of k consecutive integers is 51.
  Therefore (k/2)(2k-51) = 51.
  Solving for k gives us k = 17 or k = -3.
  Since k has to be a positive number, we can discard k = -3.
  Therefore, the answer is A: 40.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:

  Rearranging the terms, we get:
  (-50 + n-1) + (-49 + n-2) + ... + (n-2) + (n-1) = 51
  The number of terms (k) in the sum is the number of integers from -50 to n-1, inclusive.
  Using the formula for the sum of an arithmetic series, we can write:
  k/2 * (-50 + n-1) = 51
  k/2 * (n-51) = 49
  k * (n-51) = 98
  We know that k and n are positive integers.
  The only factor pairs of 98 that give a positive integer solution for n-51 are (98, 1), (49, 2), (14, 7).
  The only factor pair that gives a positive integer solution for k is (49, 2).
  Therefore, k = 49 * 2 = 98.
  The answer is D: 92.

Question: A certain liquid passes through a drain at a rate of w/25 gallons every x seconds. At that rate, how many minutes will it take y gallons to pass through the drain?
Choices:
  A: y/(1200xy)
  B: 20xy/w
  C: 5xy/(12w)
  D: w/(3xy)
  E: 3y/(wx)
Response 0:
Thought:

  Let's convert the rate to gallons per minute.
  1 minute = 60 seconds
  The rate is w/25 gallons per x seconds = (w/25) * (60/x) gallons per minute = 12w/5x gallons per minute.
  To find the time it takes for y gallons to pass through the drain, we can use the formula: time = amount/rate.
  Therefore, time = y / (12w/5x) = (5xy) / (12w)
  The answer is C: 5xy/(12w).
Action: Answer("C")

  We need to find how many minutes it will take y gallons to pass through the drain.

### Temperature: 8.0 | Problem 60 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A square piece of cloth is trimmed by 4 feet on one edge to form a rectangular piece, which is then cut diagonally in half to create two triangles. If the area of each of triangle is 70 square feet, what was the perimeter (in feet) of the original piece of square cloth?
Choices:
  A: 56
  B: 58
  C: 60
  D: 62
  E: 64
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let x be the side of the original square piece of cloth.
  Since a rectangle is formed by trimming 4 feet from one edge, the dimensions of the rectangle are x-4 and x.
  Using Pythagoras theorem, the length of the diagonal of the rectangle is sqrt[(x-4)^2 + x^2] = sqrt[2x^2 - 8x + 16].
  Since the rectangle is cut into two triangles, the area of each triangle is (1/2) * (x-4) * (sqrt[2x^2 - 8x + 16]/2) = 35.
  Simplifying this equation gives: (x-4) * (sqrt[2x^2 - 8x + 16]) = 140.
  Squaring both sides, we get: 2x^2 - 8x - 1716 = 0.
  Solving for x using the quadratic formula gives us x = 29 or x = -21 (discarding the negative root).
  Therefore, the perimeter of the original square piece of cloth is 4x = 116.
  The answer is D: 62.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Thought:
  The area of each of the triangles is 70 square feet.
  The original square piece of cloth was trimmed by 4 feet on one edge. Let's assume that the original side length of the square was "x".
  Therefore, after trimming, the new dimensions of the rectangular piece of cloth are (x-4) feet and x feet.
  The rectangular piece of cloth is then cut diagonally in half, which means we have two congruent triangles.
  The area of each triangle is (1/2) * base * height, where base and height are the dimensions of the rectangular piece of cloth that was cut diagonally.
  We know that the area of each triangle is 70 square feet, so we can set up an equation as follows:

    70 = (1/2) * (x-4) * x

  Solving for x, we get x = 10. Therefore, the original side length of the square piece of cloth was 14 feet.
  The perimeter of the original square piece of cloth is 4 * 14 = 56 feet.
  Therefore, the answer is A: 56.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 2:
Thought:
- The area of a triangle is 1/2 * base * height. 
- Since both triangles have the same area of 70 square feet, and the area of a triangle is 1/2 * base * height, we can find the base and height of one of the triangles and then double the perimeter of the original square to get the answer. 
- Let's say that the original square had a side length of x. After trimming 4 feet from one of the sides, the resulting rectangle has dimensions (x-4) by x. Using Pythagoras' theorem, the diagonal of the rectangle (which is also the hypotenuse of the two triangles) can be found to be sqrt((x-4)^2 + x^2). 
- Since the two triangles are congruent, we can say that (1/2)(x-4)(base) = 70, which simplifies to (x-4)(base) = 140. 
- We can also say that (1/2)x(height) = 70, which simplifies to x(height) = 140, or height = 140/x. 

- We can substitute height into the equation for the diagonal: 
sqrt((x-4)^2 + x^2) = sqrt(x^2 + (140/x)^2)

- We can square both sides to get rid of the square root:
(x-4)^2 + x^2 = x^2 + (140/x)^2

- Simplifying:
(x-4)^2 = (140/x)^2
x^2 - 8x + 16 = 19600/x^2
x^4 - 8x^3 + 16x^2 - 19600 = 0

- Factoring:
(x-50)(x^3 + 42x^2 - 824x + 39200) = 0

- One root is x=50, which is the side length of the original square. 
- The perimeter of the original square is 4x, or 4*50 = 200. 
- Therefore, the answer is E: 64.

Thought:
  We need to find the perimeter of the original square piece of cloth.
  Let's assume the original side length of the square is x.
  When the 4 feet of cloth was trimmed, the new rectangular piece had dimensions x-4 and x.
  The area of the rectangular piece is (x-4)x = x^2 - 4x.
  When the rectangular piece was cut diagonally in half, the two triangles formed are right triangles.
  Hence, the area of each triangle is 1/2(base*height) = 70.
  Therefore, base*height = 2(70) = 140.
  Let's call the base and height of the triangle formed by the x-4 side as b1 and h1, respectively.
  Let's call the base and height of the triangle formed by the x side as b2 and h2, respectively.
  Then, we have b1^2 + h1^2 = (x-4)^2
  and b2^2 + h2^2 = x^2.
  Also, b1*b2 = 140 (since the area of both triangles is equal).
  Adding the two equations and simplifying, we get x^2 - 4x - 56 = 0.
  Solving the quadratic equation gives x = 8 or x = -7 (we ignore the negative solution).
  So the original square piece of cloth had a side length of 8 feet.
  Therefore, the perimeter of the original square piece of cloth = 4(8) = 32 feet.

Thought:
  The area of each triangle is 70 square feet.
  If we know the area of a triangle, we can find the length of the two sides and the hypotenuse.
  Let x be the length of the rectangular piece and y be the width, then the area of the rectangular piece is xy.
  If we cut the rectangular piece diagonally into two right triangles, the area of each triangle is (1/2)xy.
  We are given that (1/2)xy = 70, so xy = 140.
  After trimming 4 feet from one edge, the rectangular piece has dimensions x-4 and y.
  Using the Pythagorean theorem, the length of the diagonal of the rectangular piece is sqrt[(x-4)^2 + y^2].
  Since we cut the rectangular piece diagonally to form two triangles, the length of the diagonal is equal to the hypotenuse of each right triangle.
  We can use the area of the triangle to find the length of the other two sides of the right triangle.
  Area = (1/2)bh = 70, so bh = 140/sqrt(2).
  The length of one of the sides of the right triangle is b = (140/sqrt(2))/h.
  The length of the other side of the right triangle is h.
  Since the length of the diagonal is the hypotenuse of the right triangle, we can use the Pythagorean theorem to find h and x.
  (x-4)^2 + y^2 = h^2
  (140/sqrt(2))^2/h^2 + h^2 = [(x-4)^2 + y^2]/h^2
  Simplifying the second equation, we get: (7056 + 2h^2)/h^2 = x^2 - 8x + 16 + y^2/h^2
  We know that xy = 140, so y = 140/x.
  Substituting y in the first equation, we get: (x-4)^2 + (140/x)^2 = h^2
  Substituting y and h in the second equation, we get: (7056 + 2(x^2 + 19600/x^2))/x^2 = x^2 - 8x + 16 + (19600/x^2)
  Simplifying the second equation, we get: 2x^4 - 8x^3 + 392x^2 - 7840 = 0
  Factoring out 2x^2, we get: 2x^2(x^2 - 4x + 1960) = 0
  The only positive solution is x = 20.
  Therefore, the perimeter of the original square cloth is 4x = 80.
  The answer is E: 64.

Action: Answer("E")

Since the area of a triangle is 1/2 * base * height, we can set up and solve an equation for x:
1/2 * (x-4) * h = 70, where h is the height of the triangle.

The perimeter of the original square piece of cloth is 4x.

Setting these two expressions equal to each other, we can solve for x:
4x = 2x - 4 + 280 / (x - 4)
Simplifying the equation gives us a quadratic equation:
2x^2 - 16x + 280 = 0
Dividing both sides by 2, we get:
x^2 - 8x + 140 = 0
Factoring the quadratic gives us:
(x - 2)(x - 6) = 0
Therefore, x = 2 or x = 6. But x cannot be 2, as the rectangular piece will have negative length. Therefore, x = 6 feet. 
So the perimeter of the original square piece of cloth is 4x = 4*6 = 24 feet.

Topic: Math
Question: A rectangular parking space is marked out by painting three of its sides. If the length of the unpainted side is 9 feet, and the sum of the lengths of the painted sides is 37 feet, then what is the area of the parking space in square feet?
Choices:
  A: 46
  B: 81
  C: 126
  D: 252
  E: None
Response 0:
Thought: 
  Let's represent the width of the parking space with "w" and length with "l".
  The sum of the lengths of the painted sides = perimeter - length of the unpainted side = 2(l + w) - 9 = 37.
  Simplifying the equation we get, l + w = 23.
  The area of the parking space = length x width = l x w.
  To solve for the area, we need to find the values of l and w.
  We have two unknowns, so we need another equation to solve the system of equations.
  We are given the length of the unpainted side, which is w = 9.
  Plugging in w = 9 into l + w = 23 we get l = 14.
  The area of the parking space = l x w = 14 x 9 = 126 square feet.
  Thus, the answer is C: 126.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
We can use the formula of the area of a rectangle to solve this problem.
The formula is A = l × w, where A is the area of the rectangle, l is the length, and w is the width.

Therefore, we can assume that the length of the rectangle is 9 feet.
The sum of the lengths of the painted sides is 37 feet, and we know that the length of the rectangle is 9 feet.
Therefore, the sum of the lengths of the two painted sides that are parallel to the length of the rectangle is 37 - 2 × 9 = 19 feet. This is the perimeter of a rectangle with length 9 and width (19/2)-9 = 5 feet.
Now we can use the formula A = l × w to calculate the area of the rectangle: A = 9 × 5 = 45 square feet.

  Then, A = W(28 - W)
  Expanding the above equation, we get A = 28W - W^2
  We know that the area cannot be negative, so we can find the maximum value of A by completing the square (i.e. by maximizing -W^2 + 28W)
  The maximum value is when W = 14, and the maximum area is A = 14*14 = 196.
  Therefore, the answer is 196 square feet, and the closest value to it is A: 46.

Question: Julie’s yard is rectangular. One side of the yard is 100 feet wide. The total area of the yard is 3,000 square feet. What is the length of the other side of the yard?
Choices:

  B: 20 feet
  C: 10 feet
  D: 50 feet
  E: 60 feet

  We also know that the total area of the yard is 3,000 square feet.

  Let L be the length of the yard.
  Then we have L x 100 = 3,000.
  Solving for L, we get L = 30.
  Therefore, the length of the other side of the yard is 30 feet.

Question: Hoses A and B spout water at different constant rates, and hose A can fill a certain pool in 8 hours. Hose A filled the pool alone for the first 2 hours and the two hoses, working together, then finished filling the pool in another 3 hours. How many hours would it have taken hose B, working alone, to fill the entire pool?
Choices:
  A: 8
  B: 15
  C: 12
  D: 6
  E: 3
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's assume the capacity of the pool is C.
  Let's rate of hose A be RA and the rate of hose B be RB.
  From the problem, we can get:
    - Hose A can fill the pool alone in 8 hours. So, in an hour, it can fill C/8 of the pool.
    - Let's assume hose B can fill the pool alone in x hours. Therefore, in an hour, it can fill C/x of the pool.
  The problem states that hose A filled the pool alone for the first 2 hours. Therefore, we have filled 2*(C/8) of the pool.
  The remaining part of the pool, i.e. (C - (2*(C/8))) will be filled by hoses A and B together.
  Together, hose A and B took 3 hours to fill the remaining part of the pool. Therefore, in an hour, they can fill (C - (2*(C/8))) / 3 of the pool.
  Now, we can form the equation as (C - (2*(C/8))) / 3 = (C/8) + (C/x)
  Solving the above equation, we get x = 24
  Therefore, hose B, working alone, would take 24 hours to fill the entire pool.
  The answer is E: 24. 
Action: Answer("E")

  Since hoses A and B working together were able to fill the pool in three hours, their combined rate is 1/3 of the pool per hour.
  It took hose A three hours to fill 3/8 of the pool.
  Therefore, the remaining volume of the pool (5/8) was filled in three hours by hoses A and B.

  1/8 + Y = 1/3
  Solving for Y, we get Y = 1/3 - 1/8 = 5/24.
  Then, using the formula rate = work/time, we have:
  5/24 = 1/X
  Solving for X, we get X = 24/5.
  Therefore, it would take hose B, working alone, 24/5 hours or 4.8 hours to fill the entire pool.

  R_B = (R_A * 8) / 24 = R_A / 3
  Therefore, hose B can fill the entire pool working alone in 8 * 3 = 24 hours.

Question: If one of the roots of the quadratic equation x^2 + mx + 22 = 0 is 1.5, then what is the value of m?
Choices:
  A: -23.5
  B: -17.5
  C: -10.5
  D: -16.2
  E: Cannot be determined
Response 0:
Thought: 
  We know that one of the roots of the quadratic equation is 1.5.
  Let's use the fact that the sum of the roots of a quadratic equation is equal to -b/a, 
  where b is the coefficient of x and a is the coefficient of x^2.
  Since one of the roots is 1.5, the other root must be -m/1.5. 
  So the sum of the roots is 1.5 + (-m/1.5) = (-b)/a.
  The sum of the roots is also equal to -m/a.
  Setting these two equations equal to each other, we get (-m/a) = (-b)/a, which implies m = -b.
  From the equation x^2 + mx + 22 = 0, we see that a = 1 and 22/a = 22. 
  Since one root is 1.5, we can use Vieta's formula to find the sum of the roots, which is -m/a = -m/1 = -m.
  Let's use the fact that the product of the roots of a quadratic equation is equal to c/a, 
  where c is the constant term in the quadratic equation.
  In this case, the product of the roots is 1.5*(-m/1.5) = -m/1 = -m.
  Setting this equal to 22/a = 22, we get -m = 22, which implies m = -22.
  The answer is A: -23.5.
Action: Answer("A")

### Temperature: 8.0 | Problem 66 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: In a large forest, 300 deer were caught, tagged, and returned during 2001. During 2002, 500 deer were caught at random, of which only 20 had tags from the previous year. If the percent of deer in the forest that had tags during the second year and were caught in the 500 deer sample is representative of the percent of the total deer population in the forest with tags, what is the total deer population in the forest (assuming no change in population between 2001 and 2002)?
Choices:
  A: 300
  B: 500
  C: 5000
  D: 6000
  E: 7500
Response 0:
Thought: 
  In 2001, 300 deer were caught, tagged, and released.
  In 2002, 500 deer were caught, out of which 20 had tags from the previous year.
  Therefore, the number of deer in the forest that had tags during the second year is 20.
  If the percent of deer in the forest that had tags during the second year and were caught in the 500 deer sample is representative of the percent of the total deer population in the forest with tags, then (20/x) = (500/y), where x is the total deer population in the forest and y is the number of deer with tags in the forest during the second year.
  Solving for y, we get y = (20 * 500)/x.
  We know that y = 20, so substituting that into the equation, we get 20 = (20 * 500)/x. Solving for x, we get x = 5000.
  Therefore, the total deer population in the forest is 5000.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
  The percent of tagged deer in the 500 deer sample is representative of the percent of the total deer population in the forest with tags.
  The number of tagged deer caught in 2002 is equal to the number of tagged deer in the forest from 2001 that were not caught in 2002 plus the number of tagged deer from 2001 that were caught in 2002. 
  Let's assume that the number of deer in the forest is "x."
  In 2001, 300 deer were tagged, which means 300 deer were tagged out of "x" deer in the forest.
  In 2002, 20 deer from the sample had tags from 2001, which means 20 tagged deer were caught out of 500 deer in the sample.
  Therefore, the proportion of tagged deer in the sample is (20/500) = (300/y), where "y" is the total deer population in the forest.
  We can solve for "y" as follows: 
  (20/500) = (300/y)
  y = (500*300)/20
  y = 7500
  Therefore, the total deer population in the forest is 7500.
  The answer is E: 7500.
Action: Answer("E")

Question: On dividing 2272 and 875 by a 3-digit number N, we get the same remainder. The sum of the digits of N is:
Choices:
  A: 10
  B: 11
  C: 12
  D: 13
  E: 14
Response 0:
Thought:
Let the remainder be x. Then:
  2272 = aN + x
  875 = bN + x
where a, b are quotients.

Subtracting the equations we get:
  1397 = (a - b)N
  
1397 is a product of 13 and 107 (1397 = 13*107). Both 13 and 107 are prime numbers, so the only possibilities for N are 13 and 107.

We can test each of them and see which one satisfies the common remainder. The sum of the digits of the number that works will be the answer.

If N = 13, then a - b = 107. 
  This means a is 107 greater than b.
  Since 2272 = 13a + x, and 875 = 13b + x, it follows that 2272 > 13a and 875 < 13b.
  It is impossible for a and b to be far apart enough to satisfy these inequalities.
  
If N = 107, then a - b = 13.
  This means a is 13 greater than b.
  Since 2272 = 107a + x, and 875 = 107b + x, it follows that 2272 > 107a and 875 < 107b.
  The only way for these inequalities to be satisfied is if a = 21 and b = 8.
  Then N = 107, and the common remainder is 57.
  The sum of the digits of N is 1 + 0 + 7 = 8.
  
Therefore, the answer is A: 10.

Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought: 
  Let's assume the 3-digit number is "abc".
  On dividing 2272 by abc, we get a remainder x. So, 2272 = k * abc + x (where k is the quotient).
  On dividing 875 by abc, we get the same remainder x. So, 875 = l * abc + x (where l is the quotient).
  We need to find the sum of digits of abc.
  Let's try to find x.
  2272 = k * abc + x
  875 = l * abc + x
  Subtracting both equations, we get:
  1397 = (k - l) * abc
  We know that 1397 is a prime number.
  Therefore, (k - l) can only be 1 or 1397.
  If (k - l) = 1, then abc = 100 * x + y and (k - l) = 1 implies that x - y = 1.
  If (k - l) = 1397, then abc = x + y + z, and (k - l) = 1397 implies that x + y + z is a multiple of 1397.
  Let's try to solve for (k - l) = 1:
  2272 = k * abc + x
  2272 = (k+1) * (abc - 1) + (x+1)
  Subtracting both equations, we get:
  k*(abc - (abc - 1)) - (x+1) = x
  k - x - 1 = x
  k = 2x + 1
  875 = l * abc + x
  875 = (l+1) * (abc - 1) + (x+1)
  Subtracting both equations, we get:
  l*(abc - (abc - 1)) - (x+1) = x
  l - x - 1 = x
  l = 2x + 1
  Now, we have:
  abc = 100 * x + y
  abc = x + y + z
  k = 2x + 1
  l = 2x + 1
  Let's try to solve for (k - l) = 1397:
  2272 = k * abc + x
  875 = l * abc + x
  Subtracting both equations, we get:
  1397 = (k - l) * abc
  1397 = (2x + 1 - 2x - 1) * abc
  1397 = 0 * abc
  This is not possible, so we can discard this case.
  Now, we need to find the sum of digits x+y+z (since (k - l) = 1).

  k = 2x + 1
  l = 2x + 1
  abc = 100 * x + y
  Substitute abc in terms of x and y:
  2272 = (2x + 1) * (100 * x + y) + x
  2272 = 200x^2 + 101x + y
  y = 2272 - 200x^2 - 101x
  875 = (2x + 1) * (100 * x + y) + x
  875 = 200x^2 + 201x + y
  y = 875 - 200x^2 - 201x
  Equating both expressions of y, we get:
  2272 - 200x^2 - 101x = 875 - 200x^2 - 201x
  1397 = 100x
  x = 13.97 (not an integer, so this is not possible)
  Therefore, there is no solution for this problem.
  The answer is "None of the Above".

### Temperature: 8.0 | Problem 69 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: By himself, Jack can clean a yacht in 12 hours. On a particular day, he happens to finish two-thirds of the work. The remaining portion of the work is done by Jill, whose rate of cleaning is just 5% of what Jack can do. How long does it take Jill to finish the remaining work?
Choices:
  A: 4
  B: 8
  C: 22
  D: 50
  E: 20
Response 0:
Thought:
  If Jack can clean a yacht in 12 hours, his rate of cleaning is 1/12 of a yacht per hour.
  On a particular day, Jack finishes two-thirds of the work. Therefore, only one-third of the work is left for Jill.
  Let's call the time Jill takes to clean one-third of the yacht t.
  Jill's rate of cleaning is 5% of Jack's rate, which is (5/100) * (1/12) = 1/240 of a yacht per hour.
  Therefore, the equation we can create is (1/240)t = (1/3) which we can solve for t to get the answer.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
Let's say the portion of the cleaning work completed by Jack is 2/3 of the total work. That means the remaining 1/3 of the work is completed by Jill.
Let's say the total time Jill takes to finish the remaining work is "t" hours.
Jack can complete the work in 12 hours. That means Jack can clean 1/12 of the yacht in an hour.
We know Jill's cleaning rate is just 5% of Jack's rate. So Jill can clean 5/100 or 1/20 of the yacht in an hour.
Using the formula: 
  Work = Rate x Time
  Let's calculate the portion cleaned by Jack in the time Jill takes to clean the remaining portion of the yacht:
  2/3 = (1/12) x (t + Jill's time)
  2/3 = t/12 + (1/20) t
  2/3 = (8t + 3t) / 120
  2/3 = 11t / 120
  t = (2/3) x (120/11)
  t ≈ 22
Therefore, Jill takes 22 hours to finish the remaining portion of the work.
The answer is C: 22.
Action: Answer("C")

Topic: Math
Question: Mr.Sam takes 17 hours to go by train to a certain city and return by car. He loses 4 hours if he goes both ways by train. How long would he have taken if he had traveled by car in both ways?
Choices:
  A: 22 hrs
  B: 18 hrs
  C: 16 hrs
  D: 20 hrs
  E: 13 hrs
Response 0:
Thought: 
  Let's assume the time taken by Mr. Sam to go to the city by train is 't' hours.
  Then, the time taken by him to return by car would be (17-t) hours.
  As per the question, if he goes both ways by train, he loses 4 hours.
  Therefore, the time taken by him to go both ways by train would be (2t + 4) hours.
  If he had traveled by car in both ways, the time taken would be (17-t) + (17-t) = 34 - 2t hours.
  Now, equating the above 2 equations, we get:
  2t + 4 = 34 - 2t
  4t = 30
  t = 15
  Therefore, the time taken by Mr. Sam to go to the city by train is 15 hours and the time taken by him to return by car would be (17 - 15) = 2 hours.
  If he had traveled by car in both ways, the time taken would be 2 x 2 = 4 hours.
  Therefore, the answer is D: 20 hrs.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Thought:
- Mr. Sam takes 17 hours for going by train to a city and returning by car.
- If he goes both ways by train, he loses 4 hours, which means the round trip by train takes 21 hours.
- Therefore, the one-way trip by train takes (21/2) = 10.5 hours.
- The one-way trip by car would take (17 - 10.5) = 6.5 hours.
- The round trip by car would take (2 x 6.5) = 13 hours.
- Therefore, Mr. Sam would take 13 hours if he had traveled by car both ways.
Action: Answer("E")
Response 2:
Thought:
  Let's denote the time taken by the train to reach the city as 'x'. Therefore, the time taken by the car to cover the same distance is (x-4) [because he loses 4 hours if he goes both ways by train].
  According to the problem, the total time taken when he goes by train and returns by car is 17. Therefore, x + (x-4) = 17.
  Solving the above equation, we get x = 10.5. Therefore, the time taken by the car to cover the same distance is (10.5-4) = 6.5.
  So, the total time taken if he had traveled by car in both ways would be 6.5*2 = 13 hrs.
  The answer is E: 13 hrs.

Response 4:
Thought:
  Let's call the time it takes Mr. Sam to go to the city by train as Tt.
  Let's call the time it takes Mr. Sam to return from the city by car as Tc.
  We know that Tt + Tc = 17 (hours).
  We also know that 2Tt - 4 = Tc. We can solve this for Tt by adding 4 and dividing by 2.
  2Tt - 4 + 4 = Tc + 4
  2Tt = Tc + 8
  2Tt = 17 - Tt + 8
  3Tt = 25
  Tt = 25/3 hours
  If he had traveled by car in both ways, the total time would be Tc + Tc = 2Tc.
  Therefore, 2Tc = 17 - 25/3 = 26/3 hours.
  The answer is D: 20 hrs.

Response 7:
Thought:
  Let's assume the speed of the train is t and the speed of the car is c.
  Then, the distance between the two cities will be the same whether Mr.Sam travels by train or car.
  Let d be the distance between the two cities.
  Since time = distance / speed, Mr.Sam took 17 hours to reach the destination by train. Therefore, d/t = 17 or d = 17t.
  The time Mr.Sam took to get back from the city by car can be expressed as d/c. Therefore, the total time he took is 17 + d/c.
  If Mr.Sam goes both ways by train, he will take 2 * 17 = 34 hours in total.
  But, he loses 4 hours if he goes by train both ways. So, the time he would have taken if he had traveled both ways by train is 34 - 4 = 30 hours.
  Therefore, (d/c) * 2 = 30, or d/c = 15.
  Substituting d = 17t, c = (17/15)t.
  Therefore, the time he takes to travel by car both ways = 2d/c = 2 * 17t / ((17/15)t) = 30 hours.
  
  The answer is D: 20 hrs.

Question: For bringing each copper coin from the bottom of a river, a coin-diver gets 20 cents, and for each brass coin she gets 25 cents. If after one dive, she got $3.40. What is the minimum number of copper coins that she brought?
Choices:
  A: 4
  B: 3
  C: 2
  D: 1
  E: 0
Response 0:
Thought: 
  Let's assume the diver brought x copper coins and y brass coins.
  From the problem, we know that for bringing each copper coin she gets 20 cents and for each brass coin she gets 25 cents. 
  Therefore, the total amount of money she made can be expressed as 20x + 25y cents.
  The problem states that after one dive, she got $3.40 or 340 cents.
  So, we have the following equation: 20x + 25y = 340.
  To find the minimum number of copper coins, we need to try different values for x and see which one gives us a whole number solution for y.
  We can start by assuming she brought 4 copper coins, then 3 copper coins, then 2 copper coins, and so on.
  When we plug in x=2, we get y=8 as a solution, which means she brought 2 copper coins and 8 brass coins.
  Therefore, the minimum number of copper coins that she brought is 2.
  The answer is C: 2.
Action: Answer("C")

### Temperature: 8.0 | Problem 72 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: The sum of the digits of a three digit number is 17, and the sum of the squares of its digits is 109. If we subtract 495 from the number, we shall get a number consisting of the same digits written in the reverse order. Find the number.
Choices:
  A: 368
  B: 377
  C: 288
  D: 997
  E: 112
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's assume that the hundreds digit is a, the tens digit is b and the units digit is c. 
  We know that a+b+c=17, and a^2+b^2+c^2=109.
  Also, the three digit number is 100a+10b+c, and the reversed number is 100c+10b+a. 
  If we subtract 495 from the original number we get 100a+10b+c-495.
  We know that (100c+10b+a) = (100a+10b+c-495), which is the same as (99a-99c)=495 or (a-c)=5. 
  Now we have two equations: a+b+c=17 and a-c=5. 
  Solving for a and c in terms of b, we get a = 6 + b and c = b - 1. 
  Substituting these values in the expression for the sum of squares of digits, we get 3b^2 - 6b + 10 = 109. 
  Solving this quadratic equation, we get b = 7 or -3/2. Since b is a digit, we ignore the negative root and get b = 7. 
  Therefore, the number is 671. 
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Let's call the three digit number "abc" where a,b,c are digits.
  We know that a+b+c=17 and a^2+b^2+c^2=109.
  We also know that (100a+10b+c)-495=100c+10b+a.
  We can simplify this equation as 99a-99c+495=99c+9a.
  Simplifying further, we get 90a-198c+495=0.
  Simplifying again, we get 5a-11c+15=0.
  a-b+c=17-2b.
  Squaring this equation, we get a^2-2ab+b^2+c^2-2bc+2ac=289-68b+4ac.
  We know that a^2+b^2+c^2=109 therefore 2ac-2bc-2ab=-68b+109-289+15=-68b-165.
  Substituting 5a-11c+15=0, we get b=3, a=6 and c=8.
  Therefore, abc=683.
  The answer is A: 368.

    x + y + z = 17
    x² + y² + z² = 109

    x = 17 - y - z

    (17 - y - z)² + y² + z² = 109

Question: The ratio of the volumes of a cube to that of the sphere which will fit inside the cube is?
Choices:
  A: 2: π
  B: 7:2
  C: 8:2
  D: 6: π
  E: 8:3
Response 0:
Thought:
  The volume of a cube is given by s^3, where s is the length of a side.
  The volume of a sphere is given by (4/3)πr^3, where r is the radius of the sphere.
  If the sphere is inscribed in the cube, then the diameter of the sphere is equal to the length of a side of the cube.
  Let s be the length of the side of the cube and r be the radius of the sphere.
  The diameter of the sphere is equal to s, so the radius is r = s/2.
  The volume of the cube is s^3.
  The volume of the sphere is (4/3)πr^3 = (4/3)π*(s/2)^3 = (4/3)(π/8)*s^3 = (π/6)*s^3.
  Therefore, the required ratio of the volumes is s^3 : (π/6)*s^3 = 6:π.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Let us assume that the edge length of the cube is 2.
  Therefore, the volume of the cube is 2³ = 8 cubic units.
  The diameter of the sphere will be equal to the edge length of the cube which is 2. Therefore, the radius will be 1.
  The volume of a sphere with radius r is given by 4/3 * π * r³.
  Therefore, the volume of the sphere will be 4/3 * π * (1)³ = 4/3 * π cubic units.
  Now, we need to find the ratio of the volumes of the cube to that of the sphere which will fit inside the cube.
  The volume of the sphere that will fit inside the cube will be equal to the volume of the cube.
  Ratio of the volumes of cube to sphere = Volume of Cube / Volume of Sphere
                                          = 8 / (4/3 * π)
                                          = 6 / π

  Therefore, the answer is D: 6: π.

  (4/3)π((s/2)^3) = (1/6)π(s^3)

Topic: Math
Question: There are ten lime soda bottles on a table in a restaurant. They are to be served among two different groups of customers consisting of 5 members each. How many ways are there to create these 2 groups?
Choices:
  A: 90
  B: 105
  C: 126
  D: 252
  E: 525
Response 0:
Thought:
  We need to find the number of ways to divide the 10 bottles into two different groups.
  The first group can have any number of bottles from 0 to 5, and the second group will have the remaining bottles.
  The number of ways to choose k items from n items is given by nCk = n!/(k!(n-k)!).
  So, the number of ways to divide the 10 lime soda bottles into two groups of 5 is given by 10C5 = 10!/(5!5!) = 252.
  Therefore, the answer is D: 252.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Thought:
  We can divide the 10 lime soda bottles into two groups in the following way:
   - First group of 5 bottles.
   - Second group of 5 bottles.
  Order within the groups doesn't matter.
  There are 10 bottles to choose from for the first group (i.e. 10 choose 5).
  After the first group has been selected, only 5 bottles remain for the second group.
  Thus, there are 5 bottles to choose from for the second group.
  Therefore, the total number of ways to create two groups of 5 bottles each is (10 choose 5) * (5 choose 5).
  (10 choose 5) = 252 and (5 choose 5) = 1.
  Therefore, the answer is 252 * 1 = 252.
Action: Answer("D")

  Therefore, the answer is 10C5 * 5C5.

### Temperature: 8.0 | Problem 76 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: All 250 files on Sam's hard drive are infected by either a virus or a worm or both. The number of files that are infected only by a worm is 2.5 times the number of files that are infected by both a virus and a worm. If 50% of the files were not infected by a virus, how many of Sam's files were NOT infected by a worm?
Choices:
  A: 50
  B: 70
  C: 75
  D: 100
  E: 125
Response 0:
Thought: 
  Let's represent the number of files that are only infected by a virus using V.
  Let's represent the number of files that are only infected by a worm using W.
  Let's represent the number of files that are infected by both a virus and a worm using B.
  We know that V + W + B = 250.
  We also know that W = 2.5B.
  We know that 50% of the files were not infected by a virus, therefore V = 0.5 x 250 = 125.
  We can substitute these values to solve for W.
  125 + W + B = 250
  Substitute W = 2.5B
  125 + 2.5B + B = 250
  3.5B = 125
  B = 35.7 (rounded to nearest whole number)
  W = 2.5 x B = 89 (rounded to nearest whole number)
  The number of files that were not infected by a worm is V + B = 125 + 35 = 160.
  The answer is E: 125.
Action: Answer("E")
Response 1:
Thought: 
  Let the number of files infected only by a virus be V, the number of files infected only by a worm be W, and the number of files infected by both a virus and a worm be X. 
  We know that V + W + X = 250, and W = 2.5X.
  Also, let the number of files not infected by a virus be Y. Since 50% of the files were not infected by a virus, we know V+X = 0.5(250) = 125.
  Substituting W = 2.5X into V + W + X = 250 and simplifying yields 3.5X = 250 - Y. 
  Substituting V + X = 125 into 3.5X = 250 - Y and simplifying yields Y = 125 - 2X.
  Therefore, we need to find X to calculate the number of files that were NOT infected by a worm.
  Solving for X, we get X = 30, so Y = 65.
  The answer is 65, so the correct choice is option A: 50.

Choices:

  B: 300

  D: 320
  E: 315

  The trader sold the article at a profit of 20% which means he sold it for 120% of its cost price.
  Selling price of the article = 120% of x = 1.2x
  We also know that the selling price of the article is Rs.360.
  Therefore, 1.2x = 360
  Solving for 'x', x = 300
  Hence, the cost price of the article is Rs.300

  Given, selling price = Rs. 360

  Therefore, the cost price of the article is Rs. 300.

Question: A newspaper costs $4 on Sunday and $1 the rest of the days of the week. If a hotel orders twice as many papers on Sunday as it does the rest of the days of the week and pays $210 per week for newspapers, how many newspapers does it buy on Monday?
Choices:
  A: 15
  B: 30
  C: 45
  D: 60
  E: 75
Response 0:
Thought:
- Let's assume that the hotel buys x newspapers on each day of the week except Sunday.
- For Sunday, the hotel buys 2x newspapers.
- We know that the cost of a Sunday newspaper is $4 and the cost of a newspaper on other days is $1.
- If the hotel buys x newspapers on a day, then the cost for that day is x*$1 = $x.
- So, the cost of newspapers bought on the rest of the days of the week is 6*$x = $6x.
- The cost of Sunday newspapers is 1*$4*2x = $8x.
- The total cost is $210.
- $6x + $8x = $210.
- $14x = $210.
- x = $210/$14 = 15.
- Therefore, the hotel buys 15 newspapers on Monday.
- The answer is A: 15.

Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Let's call the number of newspapers the hotel buys on each weekday "x".

  The hotel pays $1 for each newspaper on each weekday, so the total cost of weekday newspapers is 5 * 1 * x = 5x dollars.
  The hotel pays $210 for all newspapers, so the total cost of all newspapers is 8x + 5x = 13x dollars.
  13x = 210, so x = 210 / 13.
  To find how many newspapers the hotel buys on Monday, we just need to find "x".
  Therefore, the answer is approximately 16, which means the hotel buys 16 newspapers on Monday.
  The closest answer is A: 15.

Question: Allen starts from X, goes to Y. At the same time Bob starts from Y and goes towards X. Once Allen reaches Y he changes his direction and returns to X. Once Bob reaches X, he changes his direction and returns to Y. Throughout Allen travels at 54 kmph and Bob travels at 78kmph. By the time they meet for the second time, Bob covers 48 km more than Allen. Find the distance between X and Y.
Choices:
  A: 144km
  B: 72 km
  C: 126km
  D: 84 km
  E: 48km
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let the distance from X to Y be d.
  Let time taken for Allen to reach Y be t.
  By the time they meet for the first time, Allen travels a distance of d/2 km.
  Bob travels a distance of d/2 km in the opposite direction.
  The sum of the distance travelled by both of them is d km.
  Let the distance travelled by Bob in the first t hours be x km.
  Then distance travelled by Allen in the same t hours is d/2 - x km.
  Total distance travelled by Bob is 2x km.
  Total distance travelled by Allen is d + d/2 - 2x km.
  Time taken by Bob to travel the distance d - x km is (d - x)/78 hours.
  Time taken by Allen to travel the same distance is (d/2 + x)/54 hours.
  The above two expressions should be equal as they meet at the second time.
  Also, Bob covers 48 km more than Allen in that time.
  Therefore, d/2 - 2x + 48 = d - x
  Solving the above equation, we get x = (d-48)/4
  Substituting this value of x in the above equation, we get d = 144.
  Therefore, the distance between X and Y is 144 km.
  The answer is A: 144km.

Question: A jeep travels a certain distance taking 6 hours in the forward journey. During the return journey, it increased its speed by 12km/hr and took 4 hours. What is the distance travelled by the jeep?
Choices:
  A: 126km
  B: 144km
  C: 127km
  D: 228km
  E: 128km

  So, distance travelled = speed x time = x * 6 = 6x km
  During the return journey, the speed of the jeep increased to (x+12) km/hr.
  So, distance travelled = speed x time = (x+12) * 4 = 4x + 48 km
  We know that distance travelled during the forward journey is equal to the distance travelled during the return journey. Hence,
  6x = 4x + 48
  Solving this equation, we get x = 24 km/hr.
  Distance travelled during the forward journey = 6x = 6 * 24 = 144 km
  Therefore, the distance travelled by the jeep is 144 km.
  The answer is B: 144km.

### Temperature: 8.0 | Problem 82 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: The number of water lilies on a certain lake doubles every two days. If there is exactly one water lily on the lake, it takes 60 days for the lake to be fully covered with water lilies. In how many days will the lake be fully covered with lilies, if initially there were 64 water lilies on it?
Choices:
  A: 15
  B: 28
  C: 30
  D: 53
  E: 59
Response 0:
Thought: 
  The number of water lilies doubles every two days.
  If there is 1 water lily initially, then the number of lilies after n days is 2^n.
  If there are 64 water lilies initially, then the number of lilies after n days is 64*2^n.
  The problem states that the lake is fully covered with lilies after 60 days if there is one water lily initially.
  This means that 2^30 = 1,073,741,824 lilies are needed to fully cover the lake.
  To find the number of days it takes to reach 1,073,741,824 lilies, we solve the equation 64*2^n = 1,073,741,824 for n.
  n = log2(1,073,741,824/64) = log2(16,777,216) = 24
  Therefore, if initially there were 64 water lilies on the lake, it will take 24*2 = 48 days for the lake to be fully covered with lilies.
  The answer is D: 53.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Thought:
  If the number of lilies doubles every two days, then the growth can be modeled using an exponential function of the form f(x) = a(b)^x where a is the initial number of lilies, b is the growth factor, and x is the number of days that have passed.
  If there is exactly one lily on the first day (x=0), then the function becomes f(x) = (1)(2)^(x/2) = 2^(x/2).
  If it takes 60 days for the lake to be fully covered when f(60) = 2^30 = N, then N = 2^30 represents the final number of lilies.
  If initially there were 64 lilies, then f(0) = 2^6 = 64.
  We need to find x such that f(x) = 2^30. Therefore, 2^(x/2) = 2^30/2^6 = 2^24.
  Taking the logarithm of both sides, (x/2)log(2) = 24log(2), which simplifies to x = 48.
  Therefore, the lake will be fully covered with lilies in 48 days from the initial 64 lilies.
  The answer is not one of the choices given. 
  However, the closest answer is D: 53 days.

  If there was one water lily initially, it takes 60 days for the lake to be fully covered.
  This means that the number of water lilies doubles 30 times (since 2^30 is greater than the number of water lilies needed to cover the lake).
  We need to calculate how many days it will take for there to be at least 64 * 2^30 water lilies on the lake.
  If there were 64 water lilies initially, then the lake needs to be covered by 64 * 2^30 water lilies to be fully covered.
  We can solve for the number of days using the formula: 64 * 2^(n/2) = 64 * 2^30
  Simplifying, we get: 2^(n/2) = 2^30
  Therefore, n/2 = 30
  So n = 60.
  The lake will be fully covered with lilies in 60 days if there were 64 water lilies initially.
  The answer is E: 59.  (Note that 59 is the number of days it takes to have 32 * 2^30 lilies, which is not enough to fully cover the lake. So the answer must be less than 59 days.)

Question: A train M leaves City A at 5 am and reaches City B at 9am. Another train N leaves City B at 7am and reaches City A at 1030am. At what time do the 2 trains cross one another?
Choices:
  A: 1 hr 23 min
  B: 1 hr 15 min
  C: 1 hr 8 min
  D: 56 min
  E: 55 min
Response 0:
Thought:
- Train M travels for 4 hours to reach city B. 
- Train N travels for 3.5 hours to reach city A.
- Let's suppose they meet x hours after Train N leaves City B.
- Then, Train M travels for x hours and Train N travels for (x+2) hours.
- The distance travelled by both trains is the same.
- Speed equals distance over time. 
- We can use this information to form an equation and solve for x to determine when they meet. 

Calculation:
- Train M's speed = distance / time = d / 4
- Train N's speed = distance / time = d / 3.5
- Let x be the time when both trains meet.
- Distance travelled by Train M = Train M's speed * x = dx / 4
- Distance travelled by Train N = Train N's speed * (x+2) = d(x+2) / 3.5
- Since they meet at some point in between the two cities, the sum of the distances travelled by both trains is equal to the distance between the two cities.
- Therefore, dx / 4 + d(x+2) / 3.5 = d
- Solving for x, we get x = 7/4 hours or 1 hour and 45 minutes.
- Since Train N left City B at 7 am, the two trains meet at 8:45 am (7:00 + 1:45).

Question: The average (arithmetic mean) of the weight of 10 vehicles is 12.2 tons. The average weight of the group of vehicles increased by 2.6 tons after a new heavy duty truck was added to the group? What is the weight in tons of the heavy duty truck?
Choices:
  A: 40.8
  B: 41.6
  C: 42.2
  D: 43.5
  E: 44.8
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let x be the weight of the heavy duty truck.
  The sum of the weights of the 10 vehicles before the new truck was added is 10 * 12.2 = 122
  The sum of the weights of the 11 vehicles after the new truck was added is 11 * (12.2 + 2.6) = 154.8
  The weight of the heavy duty truck is the difference between the two sums, which is 154.8 - 122 = 32.8.
  Therefore, the weight of the heavy duty truck is 32.8 tons.
Action: Answer("None of the Above") 

Note: None of the given choices match the computed value. The correct answer is 32.8 tons.
Response 1:
Thought:
  Let's assume the total weight of the 10 vehicles before adding the heavy duty truck was "x" tons.
  So, the average weight of the 10 vehicles = x/10.
  According to the problem, the average weight of the group increased by 2.6 tons after adding the new heavy duty truck.
  Therefore, the total weight of the new group of vehicles = (x + weight of the heavy duty truck) + 2.6 * 11 (11 represents the number of vehicles in the new group).
  The new average weight of the group of vehicles is (x + weight of the heavy duty truck + 2.6 * 11) / 11.
  Equating the two averages, we get:
  x/10 = (x + weight of the heavy duty truck + 2.6 * 11) / 11 - > 11x = 10(x + weight of the heavy duty truck + 2.6 * 11) -> 11x = 10x + 10 * weight of the heavy duty truck + 10 * 2.6 -> weight of the heavy duty truck = (11x - 10x - 26) / 10.
  Given that the average (arithmetic mean) of the weight of 10 vehicles is 12.2 tons, we can substitute x = 122 (12.2 * 10).
  Therefore, weight of the heavy duty truck = (11x - 10x - 26) / 10 = (11 * 122 - 10 * 122 - 26) / 10 = 42.2.
  So, the weight of the heavy duty truck is 42.2 tons.
  The answer is C: 42.2.

Question: 10kg of a mixture contains 30% sand and 70% clay. In order to make the mixture contain equal quantities of clay and sand how much of the mixture is to be removed and replaced with pure sand?
Choices:
  A: 10/7
  B: 20/7
  C: 30/7
  D: 40/7
  E: 50/7
Response 0:
Thought:
  A 10kg mixture contains 3kg of sand (30% of 10kg) and 7kg of clay (70% of 10kg).
  Let 'x' represent the amount (in kg) of mixture to be removed and replaced with pure sand.
  The new mixture will also be 10kg but will contain an equal quantity of sand and clay.
  If x kg of mixture is replaced with pure sand, then 3kg of sand + (x kg of sand) = 5kg of sand will be present in the new mixture.
  The remaining (10-x) kg of mixture will contain 7kg of clay and (10-x-3)  = (7-x) kg of sand.
  In order for the new mixture to contain equal quantities of sand and clay, 7-x = 5, or x = 2kg.
  Therefore, 2kg of the original mixture should be removed and replaced with pure sand.
  The answer is A: 10/7.
Action: Answer("A")

  - The new amount of sand in the mixture will be 3kg + x kg (the initial amount of sand plus the amount of pure sand added).
  - The new amount of clay in the mixture will be 7kg - x kg (the initial amount of clay minus the amount of mixture removed).
  - We want the mixture to have equal quantities of clay and sand, so we want:
    - 3kg + x kg = 7kg - x kg
    - Solving for x, we get:
      - 2x = 4
      - x = 2
- Therefore, we need to remove 2kg of the mixture and replace it with 2kg of pure sand.
- The total weight of the mixture after the replacement will be 10kg - 2kg + 2kg = 10kg.
- Answer is A: 10/7

Choices:

  B: 64543
  C: 74325
  D: 65000
  E: 97656
Response 0:
Thought:
  We need to arrange 2 letters followed by 2 numbers to form a bike number.
  The total number of possible letters is 26.
  The total number of possible digits is 10.
  We can arrange the two letters in 26P2 ways and two numbers in 10P2 ways.
  So, the total number of distinct bike numbers that can be formed can be given by (26P2) * (10P2).
  The number of letters that need to be distinct is 2.
  Let's calculate the value.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:

  There are 26 options for the first letter and 26 options for the second letter.
  There are 10 options for the first digit and 10 options for the second digit.
  Therefore, the total number of distinct bike numbers can be formed is:
  26 * 26 * 10 * 10 = 67,600
  We need both letters to be distinct.
  Therefore, we have to choose 2 letters out of 26, which can be done in 26C2 ways.
  Therefore, the number of distinct ways of choosing 2 letters is:
  26C2 = (26!)/[(2!)(24!)] = (26 * 25)/2 = 325

Question: What will be the cost of gardening 1-metre – broad boundary around a rectangular plot having perimeter of 340 metres at the rate of 10 per square metre?
Choices:
  A: 3400
  B: 1700
  C: 3440
  D: Cannot be determined
  E: None of these
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's use the formula for the perimeter of a rectangle: 2l + 2w = P, where l is the length and w is the width, and P is the perimeter.
  If P = 340, then 2l + 2w = 340
  We can simplify this equation to l + w = 170
  If we add 2 to both l and w to account for the 1-meter boundary, then the new equation becomes: l + 2 + w + 2 = 174
  Simplifying this, we get l + w + 4 = 174
  Therefore, l + w = 170
  The area of the rectangle is l*w, and the area of the rectangle plus the 1-meter boundary is (l+2)*(w+2)
  The area of the 1-meter boundary will be [(l+2)*(w+2)] - (l*w)
  The cost of the gardening will be the area of the 1-meter boundary multiplied by the rate of 10 per square meter.
  Let's solve for the area of the 1-meter boundary and multiply it by 10 to get the cost of gardening.
  If we substitute l+w=170, then we get the area of the 1-meter boundary is (174*168) - (170*166) = 672
  Multiplying the area by the rate of 10 per square meter, we get the cost of gardening to be 6720.
  Therefore, the answer is A: 3400.
Action: Answer("A")

  342 = 2 * (length + 2 + width + 2)

  length + width = 167

  Area = length * width

  We can use the formula: (a - b)^2 = a^2 - 2ab + b^2 to find length^2 and width^2
  (length - width)^2 = length^2 - 2 * length * width + width^2
  We know that (length - width) = sqrt((length + width)^2 - 4 * length * width)
  So, (length - width)^2 = (167 - 2 * sqrt(original area))^2 = length^2 - 2 * length * width + width^2

  The cost of gardening 1 square metre is given as $10, and the total area that needs gardening is 344 square meters.
  Therefore, the cost of gardening the entire plot will be:
      Cost = 344 * 10
           = 3440
  The answer is C: 3440.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 8:
Thought:
  The rectangular plot has a perimeter of 340 meters.
  The perimeter of a rectangle is the sum of all its sides.
  We know that 2(length + breadth) = 340.
  We need to find the area of the rectangular plot by using the formula: Area = length × breadth.
  The breadth of the rectangular plot will be decreased due to the gardening around the boundary, which will be 1 meter broad. So, the breadth will be decreased by 2 meters and the length will be decreased by 2 meters.
  The new perimeter of the rectangular plot will be 336 meters (340-4).
  We can solve the equation 2(length + breadth) = 336 to get length + breadth = 168.
  We know that Area = length × breadth.
  We can solve for Area and multiply by the rate of 10 per square meter to get the cost of gardening.
  Therefore, the answer is A: 3400.

  L+W = 170
  Also, the length and width of the rectangular plot including the garden plot will be (L+2) and (W+2), respectively.
  Therefore, the area of the garden = Area of (L+2) * (W+2) - Area of L * W
  Area of the garden = (L+2) * (W+2) - L * W
  Area of the garden = 2(L+W) + 4
  Area of the garden = 2(170) + 4
  Area of the garden = 344
  Total cost of gardening = Area of the garden * Rate per square metre
  Total cost of gardening = 344 * 10
  Total cost of gardening = 3440
  Therefore, the cost of gardening a 1-meter broad boundary around a rectangular plot having a perimeter of 340 metres at the rate of 10 per square metre would be 3440.

  Profit percentage = (Profit/Cost price) × 100
  = (2.5/5) × 100
  = 50%.
  Therefore, the percentage gain of the merchant is 50%.

### Temperature: 8.0 | Problem 93 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Joe's age, Joe's sister's age and Joe’s fathers age sums up to 100. When Joe is as old as his father, Joe's sister will be twice as old as now. When Joe is as old as his father then his father is twice as old as when his sister was as old as her father. Find the age of Joe's father?
Choices:
  A: 45
  B: 48
  C: 50
  D: 55
  E: 58
Response 0:
Thought:
Let's call Joe's age "J", his sister's age "S", and his father's age "F".
From the first statement we are given:
  J + S + F = 100

From the second statement we are given:
  J + (F - J) = F
Simplifying this equation we get:
  J = F - J

Substituting this equation into the first equation we get:
  (F - J) + S + F = 100
Simplifying this equation we get:
  2F - J + S = 100

From the third statement we are given:
  F - J = S  (when Joe is as old as his father then his father is twice as old as when his sister was as old as her father)

Substituting that last equation into the second equation we get:
  J = (F - S)/2

Substituting both of those last two equations into the third equation we get:
  F - (F - S)/2 = S
Simplifying this equation we get:
  F - F/2 + S/2 = S
  F/2 + S/2 = S
  F/2 = S/2
  F = S

Substituting F = S back into the first equation we get:
  J + 2F = 100
  J + 2S = 100
  J = 100 - 2S

Substituting this last equation into the second equation we get:
  100 - 2S + F = 2S
  F = 4S - 100

Now we can solve for F:
  F = 4S - 100
  F = 4(20) - 100
  F = 20

The age of Joe's father is 20.
Action: Answer("None of the Above")
Response 1:
Thought:
Let's use the following variables:
- Joe's age = J
- Joe's sister's age = S
- Joe’s fathers age = F

From the first piece of information, we know:
J + S + F = 100

From the second piece of information, we know:
When J = F, S + (F - S) * 2

Simplifying:
2F - S = S + 2F - 2S
3S = F

From the third piece of information, we know:
When J = F, F = 2(F - S)

Simplifying:
F = 2S

Substituting 3S for F in the first equation:
J + S + 3S = 100
4S = 100
S = 25

Substituting 25 for S in the second and third equations:
3S = F
F = 2S = 50

Therefore, the age of Joe's father is 50.
Answer: Answer("C")
Response 2:
Thought:
  Let's say x is Joe's age, y is Joe's sister's age, and z is Joe's father's age.
  From the first statement we know that x + y + z = 100.
  From the second statement we know that when x = z, y + (z - y) * 2 = 2y.
  Simplifying, we get z - y = y, which means z = 2y.
  From the third statement we know that when x = z, z = 2 * (y - z).
  Simplifying, we get y = (3/4)z.
  Substituting z = 2y and y = (3/4)z into x + y + z = 100 and solving for z, we get z = 48.
  Therefore, the age of Joe's father is 48.

Response 6:
Thought:
  Let x, y, and z be Joe's age, Joe's sister's age, and Joe's father's age, respectively.
  We know that x + y + z = 100.
  When Joe is as old as his father, y + (z - x) = 2y.
  Simplifying this equation gives z - x = y.
  When Joe is as old as his father, z - x = 2(y - z).
  Simplifying this equation gives x + z = 2y.
  Substituting z - x = y into x + z = 2y equation gives 2z = 3y.
  Substituting 2z/3 for y in x + y + z = 100 gives x + (2z/3) + z = 100.
  Simplifying this equation gives x = 100 - (5z/3).
  Since x, y, and z are all positive integers, we know that 5z/3 < 100, which means z < 60.
  By testing z values, we see that only z = 50 satisfies the equation 2z = 3y.
  Therefore, Joe's father's age is z = 50.

- Let's assume that Joe is currently "j" years old. 
- Let's assume that Joe's sister is currently "s" years old.
- Let's assume that Joe's father is currently "f" years old.
- We know that j + s + f = 100
- We know that j + f = 2(s + x) [where x is the number of years until Joe is as old as his father]
- We know that f = 2(s + y) [where y is the number of years until Joe is as old as his father]
- We need to solve for f

Solution:
- Rearranging the first equation to get s = 100 - j - f
- Substituting s into the second equation: 
j + f = 2((100 - j - f) + x)
j + f = 200 - 2j - 2f + 2x
3j + 3f = 200 + 2x
j + f = (200 + 2x)/3

- Substituting s into the third equation:
f = 2((100 - j - f) + y)
f = 200 - 2j - 2f + 2y
3f = 200 - 2j + 2y
f = (200 - 2j + 2y)/3

- Equating both expressions for f and solving for j:
(200 + 2x)/3 = (200 - 2j + 2y)/3
200 + 2x = 200 - 2j + 2y
2x + 2j - 2y = 0
x + j - y = 0
j = x + y

- Substituting j into the first equation:
(x+y) + s + f = 100
s + f = 100 - x - y

- Substituting the above equation into the third equation:
f = 2(s + y) = 2(100 - j - f + y)
f = 200 - 2j - 2f + 2y
3f = 200 - 2j + 2y
3f = 200 - 2(x+y) + 2y
f = (400 - 2x) / 5

- Substituting f into any of the previous equations to solve for x or y:
f = (200 - 2j + 2y)/3
(400 - 2x) / 5 = (200 - 2(x+y) + 2y)/3
1200 - 6x = 1000 - 6x + 6y
6y = 200
y = 200/6 = 33.33

- Substituting y into the expression for f:
f = (400 - 2x) / 5
f = (400 - 2(x+33.33)) / 5
f = (400 - 2x - 66.66) / 5
f = (333.34 - 2x) / 5

- We know that f is an integer, so we need to find the value of x that makes f an integer:
333.34 - 2x = 5n [where n is an integer]
2x = 333.34 - 5n
x = (333.34 - 5n)/2

- We need to find a value of n that makes x an integer:
when n = 66, x = (333.34 - 5(66))/2 = 50.02
when n = 67, x = (333.34 - 5(67))/2 = 48.02

Answer: Answer("B")
Response 8:
Thought:
  Let's assume Joe's age to be "J", his sister's age to be "S" and his father's age to be "F".
  From the first statement, we know J + S + F = 100.
  From the second statement, we know that when Joe is as old as his father, we get the following equation:
  J + F = 2(S + x) where x is the number of years until Joe is as old as his father.
  Simplifying this equation, we get J + F = 2S + 2x.

  From the third statement, we know that when Joe is as old as his father, his father is twice as old as when his sister was as old as her father. This gives us the equation:

  F + x = 2(S + F - S) = 2F - 2S

  Simplifying this equation, we get F + x = 2F - 2S which means x = F - 2S.

  Now we have two equations with two unknowns:
  J + S + F = 100
  J + F = 2S + 2(F - 2S)

  We can substitute the second equation into the first one, which gives us:

  J + S + F = 100
  J + F = 2F - 2S + 2F - 4S
  J + F = 4F - 6S

  Simplifying this equation, we get:

  J = 3F - 6S

  Now we can substitute this equation into the first one:

  3F - 5S + F = 100

  Simplifying this equation, we get:

  4F - 5S = 100

  We know that F, S, and J are positive integers, so we can start by guessing values for F. The only value that works is F = 45. 

  Plugging F = 45 into the equation 4F - 5S = 100, we get S = 28. Then, using J = 100 - F - S, we get J = 27.

  Therefore, Joe's father is 45 years old.

### Temperature: 8.0 | Problem 94 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Christopher and Jonathan were having bets. They decide that a coin will be flipped twenty times and each time it turns heads, Christopher will give $2 to Jonathan and each time it turns out to be Tails, Jonathan will give 3$ to Christopher. After flipping for twenty times none of the both won or lost any amount.
How many times did the coin landed on Heads ?
Choices:
  A: 10
  B: 23
  C: 16
  D: 18
  E: 12
Response 0:
Thought:
  Each time the coin lands on Heads, Christopher gives $2 to Jonathan.
  Each time the coin lands on Tails, Jonathan gives $3 to Christopher.
  After flipping the coin 20 times, no one won or lost any money.
  This means the total amount of money that Christopher gave to Jonathan is equal to the total amount of money that Jonathan gave to Christopher.
  Let's use H to represent a flip that lands on Heads, and T to represent a flip that lands on Tails.
  The total number of flips is 20, so we have: H + T = 20
  Let's say the number of times the coin lands on Heads is x, then the number of times it lands on Tails is 20 - x.
  The total amount of money that Christopher gives Jonathan is 2x, and the total amount of money that Jonathan gives Christopher is 3(20 - x) = 60 - 3x.
  Since no one won or lost any money, we have: 2x = 60 - 3x
  Solving for x, we get: x = 12.
  Therefore, the coin landed on Heads 12 times.

  Since neither of them won or lost any amount, the total amount of money won by Christopher and Jonathan should be equal.
  Therefore, the number of times the coin landed on heads should be equal to the number of times the coin landed on tails in order for the net gain/ loss of money to be zero.
  We can use algebra to solve for the number of times the coin landed on heads. 
  Let's assume that the number of times the coin landed on heads is x.
  Then, the number of times the coin landed on tails is 20-x.
  The total amount of money won by Christopher is 2x - 3(20-x) = -x - 60.
  The total amount of money won by Jonathan is 3(20-x) - 2x = 60-x.
  Since neither of them won or lost any amount, the total amount of money won by Christopher and Jonathan should be equal.
  Therefore, we can set -x-60 = 60-x and solve for x.
  The solution is x = 10.
  Therefore, the number of times the coin landed on heads is 10.

### Temperature: 8.0 | Problem 95 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Kevin drove from A to B at a constant speed of 70 mph. Once he reached B, he turned right around with pause, and returned to A at a constant speed of 90 mph. Exactly 3 hours before the end of his trip, he was still approaching B, only 70 miles away from it. What is the distance between A and B?
Choices:
  A: 180
  B: 90
  C: 270
  D: 360
  E: None of the above
Response 0:
Thought: 
  Kevin drove at a constant speed of 70 mph from A to B.
  After reaching B, he turned right around with pause, and drove at a constant speed of 90 mph from B to A.
  Exactly 3 hours before the end of his trip, he was still approaching B, only 70 miles away from it.
  This means that before the last 3 hours of his trip, he had traveled 70 miles from A towards B.
  Let's first find the time that Kevin traveled from A to B: distance = speed x time. Since d = rt, time = distance / speed.
  Let's denote the distance from A to B as d. The time it took Kevin to travel from A to B at 70 mph is t1 = d / 70.
  From B to A he traveled for (total time - t1 - 3) hours at 90 mph, because he was instructed to return to A. 
  The total time he spent on the trip is t2 = (d / 70) + (d / 90).
  We know that 3 hours before the end of his trip, he was 70 miles away from B. So the distance that he traveled from A to the point where he was 3 hours before the end of the trip is d - 70.
  We can now create an equation: (d - 70) = (90/60)(t2 - 3).
  We know that t2 = (d / 70) + (d / 90). We can substitute this into our equation: (d - 70) = (90/60)(d / 70 + d / 90 - 3).
  Simplifying this equation will give us the distance between A and B.

Topic: Math
Question: An organization decided to raise Rs. 6 lakh by collecting equal contribution from each of its employees. If each of them had contributed Rs. 60 extra, the contribution would have been Rs. 6.24 lakh. How many employees are there in that organization?
Choices:
  A: 300
  B: 200
  C: 400
  D: 100
  E: 500
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's assume there are n employees in the organization.
  If each of them contributed equally, then their contribution per person would be (6 lakh)/n
  If each of them had contributed Rs. 60 extra, the contribution per person would be ((6.24 lakh)/n) = ((6 lakh)/n) + 60
  By solving these equations, we can find the value of n.
  Rearranging, we get (6.24 lakh) = (6 lakh) + 60n
  Simplifying, we get 24000 = 60n
  Hence, n = 400
  Therefore, there are 400 employees in the organization.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
Let’s assume the number of employees in the organization is x.
Let's also assume the equal contribution from each employee is y.
From the problem, we know:
  xy = 6,00,000   ---- (1)
  (y + 60)x = 6,24,000  ---- (2)
Solving equation 1 and 2, we get:
  x = 400
Therefore, there are a total of 400 employees in the organization.

Question: A man divides Rs 8600 among 5 sons, 4 daughters and 2 nephews. If each daughter receives four times as much as each nephew, and each son receives five as much as each nephew. How much does each daughter receive ?
Choices:
  A: Rs 400
  B: Rs 500
  C: Rs 600
  D: Rs 700
  E: Rs 800
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let the amount each nephew receives be x.
  Then each daughter receives 4x and each son receives 5x.
  The total number of children receiving money is 11 (5+4+2=11).
  The total amount of money is Rs 8600.
  Therefore, we can form an equation: 5(5x) + 4(4x) + 2(x) = 8600.
  Solving for x, we get x = 100.
  Therefore, each daughter receives 4x = Rs 400.
  The answer is A: Rs 400.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
Let 'x' be the share of each nephew.
Then, the share of each daughter is 4x and the share of each son is 5x.
The total number of people who get a share is 5+4+2=11
The sum of the shares of all people is Rs 8600.

From this, we can form the equation:
5x+4(4x)+2x = 8600
Simplifying the equation:
21x = 8600
x = 400

Therefore, the share of each daughter is 4x = 4(400) = 1600.

Question: A student instead of finding the value of 7/8 of a number, found the value of 7/18 of the number. If his answer differed from the actual one by 770, find the that number.
Choices:
  A: 1584
  B: 2520
  C: 1728
  D: 1656
  E: None

  Simplifying, we get (35/72)x = 770.
  Solving for x will give us the value of the number.
  x = (770*72)/35 = 1584.
  Therefore, the answer is A: 1584.

### Temperature: 8.0 | Problem 100 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Calculate the maximum distance you can travel with $8.50 on a cab which charges $3.50 for the first quarter-mile and 10 cents for each additional quarter mile.
Choices:
  A: 11.75 miles
  B: 12.75 miles
  C: 17.75 miles
  D: 14.75 miles
  E: 10.75 miles
Response 0:
Thought:
  Every ride starts at $3.50, which means the first 0.25 miles is already covered.
  The remaining amount of money is $5.00.
  Every additional 0.25 miles costs 10 cents.
  Therefore, the maximum distance that can be covered is (amount of money remaining) / (cost per quarter-mile) + (first 0.25 miles).
  The calculation will be $5.00 divided by $0.10 per quarter-mile which equals 50 quarter-miles.
  Adding the initial quarter-mile, the total distance is 50.25 quarter-miles.
  Converting the quarter-miles to miles, we get 12.5625 miles.
  Therefore, the maximum distance that can be traveled is 12.5625 miles, which rounds to 12.75 miles. 
  The answer is B: 12.75 miles.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
